  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2004d52a-f3cf-4de6-8591-df3a8064afd2'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText6492293101797048288" style="display:none">In the epic next chapter of Soman Chainani’s New York Times bestselling series, The School for Good and Evil, everything old is new again as Sophie and Agatha fight the past as well as the present to find the perfect end to their story.<br /><br />As A World Without Princes closed, the end was written and former best friends Sophie and Agatha went their separate ways. Agatha was whisked back to Gavaldon with Tedros and Sophie stayed behind with the beautiful young School Master.<br /><br />But as they settle into their new lives, their story begs to be re-written, and this time, theirs isn’t the only one. With the girls apart, Evil has taken over and the villains of the past have come back to change their tales and turn the world of Good and Evil upside down.<br /><br />Readers around the world are eagerly awaiting the third book in The School for Good and Evil series, The Last Ever After. This extraordinary new journey delivers more action, adventure, laughter, romance and fairy tale twists and turns than you could ever dream of!</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_25261128').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18437629314424220614">HOLY CRAP HOLY CRAP HOLY CRAP HOLY CRAP<br/><br/>THIS BOOK WAS PERFECTION. IT WAS EVERYTHING SOMAN PROMISED IT WILL BE EXCELT FIVE TIMES MORE THAN THAT. <br/><br/>THE CLOSING LINE WAS PERFECT.<br/><br/>Now to the calm portion:<br/><br/>The first two books had this pattern of Sophie and Agatha being placed in a situation of injustice and pointing out said injustice within seconds. This book, however, took it a step further by having EVERYONE who experienced injustice in the course of the series call BS, including Lesso, Dot, Hester, an</span>
  <span id="freeText18437629314424220614" style="display:none">HOLY CRAP HOLY CRAP HOLY CRAP HOLY CRAP<br /><br />THIS BOOK WAS PERFECTION. IT WAS EVERYTHING SOMAN PROMISED IT WILL BE EXCELT FIVE TIMES MORE THAN THAT. <br /><br />THE CLOSING LINE WAS PERFECT.<br /><br />Now to the calm portion:<br /><br />The first two books had this pattern of Sophie and Agatha being placed in a situation of injustice and pointing out said injustice within seconds. This book, however, took it a step further by having EVERYONE who experienced injustice in the course of the series call BS, including Lesso, Dot, Hester, and even Hort (who, in my opinion, had his importance ranking skyrocket, as his role in this book was crucial to the development of all the main characters).<br /><br />This book talks about everything from fat-shaming (Dot gets a monologue, and it is ON POINT) to the blood feuds that riddled all of the Evil character's stories. And it did it in such a beautiful way, everyone should learn from what this book has to say.<br /><br />We got to know everyone so much better, and i en ended up taking a liking to a character that I formerly thought had the personality of cardboard.<br /><br />I could go on, but frankly then I'd just start spoiling the whole book, so I'll leave you all with JUST READ THIS GODDAMN BOOK.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5477217605173527287" style="display:none">BEWARE PLOT TWISTS EVERYWHERE!!!!<br />The Perfect Fairytale Ending.<br />This is my all time favorite Juvenile series. Mr. Chainani has forever filled my High School girl heart with good and happiness. If a person creates a series that was meant for juveniles and hooks a high schooler to the point of her dying for the book releases, buying his books, crying at his books and even having it as her phone wallpaper.. Well that person deserves a medal. <br /><br />Once Upon A Time there was a girl named Kylie who fell in love with a book with a gorgeous cover and interesting synopsis. <br />She started reading this book and fell in love with one of the main characters. A spunky, hilarious tomboy named Agatha. Soon a handsome yet sometimes foolish boy named Tedros entered Agatha's life. Kylie was first skeptical about this new couple, but as time went on she shipped them like she never did before and wanted Agatha to be the next queen of Camelot with Tedros as her king.<br />Then theres Sophie. Backstabbing, selfish, annoying, girly, AND EVIL, Kylie did not like her AT ALL. She couldn't stand the way Sophie would do anything to get a gorgeous boy who she didn't even love. She never hated a character more than she did Sophie.</span>

<div id="review_1374698909" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1374698909" />
    <a title="Case" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5857851-case"><img alt="Case" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383253226p2/5857851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1374698909?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Case" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Case" href="/user/show/5857851-case">Case</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24465254-the-last-ever-after">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1374698909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6627094796840227857">Do you ever read a book and have such high hopes, see so much potential...only for it to take you on a ridiculous, nonsensical runaround, completely wasting your time?<br/><br/>Yeah, that's pretty much what you're setting yourself up for if you read this book. The pacing is terrible, the characters motivations don't make any sense and the "big twist" revealed in the final pages of the book has absolutely no bearing on the outcome of the story.<br/><br/>In the first book, we're told that you can find love outside of</span>
  <span id="freeText6627094796840227857" style="display:none">Do you ever read a book and have such high hopes, see so much potential...only for it to take you on a ridiculous, nonsensical runaround, completely wasting your time?<br /><br />Yeah, that's pretty much what you're setting yourself up for if you read this book. The pacing is terrible, the characters motivations don't make any sense and the "big twist" revealed in the final pages of the book has absolutely no bearing on the outcome of the story.<br /><br />In the first book, we're told that you can find love outside of romance; that friendship is just as valuable. You don't need a prince to be happy, and it's okay to question the traditional idea of a fairy tale.<br /><br />In the second book, the author apparently changed his mind on this, pitting girls against boys and blaming the feud on the two girls who chose each other over a boy in the previous book. He turned the entire school for girls into man-hating "feminazis" and set the two leads against each other, even though they'd resolved their differences in the first book.<br /><br />The third book feels like a pathetic attempt at repairing all the damage the second did. Even after finishing the book, I'm not 100% clear on the message he was trying to send. The secondary characters were interesting and watching various characters come to terms with their parents was nice, but none of it was enough to save this insipid book from being an utter waste of time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6627094796840227857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer5774800626627641873">2017 Reread: Okay, so maybe the flaws stick out to me a bit too much the second time round! Everyone's speech, including all the secondary characters, are m o n o l o g u e s. I understand why this book is 650 pages long, because everyone speaks in paragraphs, not sentences. Also, the relationship development between Sophie and Agatha doesn't really happen until 500 pages in. The rest is just a repetition of the antics we've seen in the first two books.<br/><br/>I think it would almost be more interesting</span>
  <span id="freeText5774800626627641873" style="display:none">2017 Reread: Okay, so maybe the flaws stick out to me a bit too much the second time round! Everyone's speech, including all the secondary characters, are m o n o l o g u e s. I understand why this book is 650 pages long, because everyone speaks in paragraphs, not sentences. Also, the relationship development between Sophie and Agatha doesn't really happen until 500 pages in. The rest is just a repetition of the antics we've seen in the first two books.<br /><br />I think it would almost be more interesting to read a prequel about the story of Lady Lesso and Clarissa Dovey because they're like the OG Sophie and Agatha. <br /><br />That being said, I am pumped for Quests for Glory, especially after skimming my way through the Handbook for the clues of what's to come. I guess after two years, though, I'll definitely be changing my rating. <br /><br />2015: I love this series so much, I'm willing to look past the flaws the final book presented. The development of Agatha and Sophie's relationship is magical, everything about this book is magical in fact. I can't believe I've reached The End of this happily ever after!</span>

<div id="review_1342528025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1342528025" />
    <a title="Christina Bandiera" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33213761-christina-bandiera"><img alt="Christina Bandiera" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437770866p2/33213761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1342528025?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina Bandiera" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina Bandiera" href="/user/show/33213761-christina-bandiera">Christina Bandiera</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone who likes a good/evil fairytale, young and old!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=unputdownable">unputdownable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=fairytale-retellings">fairytale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=loooooooooooooooooooong">loooooooooooooooooooong</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=150k-200k">150k-200k</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=childhood-faves">childhood-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=boarding-schools">boarding-schools</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=fantasy-fiction">fantasy-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=laugh-out-loud-funny">laugh-out-loud-funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33213761-christina-bandiera?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1342528025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1349215162194291827">The best thing about this book (and the series as a whole, in fact) is how often it surprises you. There were many points while reading 'The Last Ever After' that I thought "How on earth are they possibly going to get out of this situation?" or "What on earth is really going on here?" only to find myself, pages or chapters later, wondering, "How on earth did I not work it out?!?!?!". The best twists, I think, are those you didn't work out but, when they are presented to you, they make perfect se</span>
  <span id="freeText1349215162194291827" style="display:none">The best thing about this book (and the series as a whole, in fact) is how often it surprises you. There were many points while reading 'The Last Ever After' that I thought "How on earth are they possibly going to get out of this situation?" or "What on earth is really going on here?" only to find myself, pages or chapters later, wondering, "How on earth did I not work it out?!?!?!". The best twists, I think, are those you didn't work out but, when they are presented to you, they make perfect sense - to the point you feel silly for not working them out sooner. 'The Last Ever After' is full of such twists and I lost count of how many times I shook my head in wonder at Soman Chainani's ability to leave me stunned.<br /><br />Some great characters are introduced in this book. Whimsical Merlin, with his wonderful hat (I want one!) was probably my favourite new character. Rafal, on the other hand, was probably my least favourite new character (or, well, sort of new, I guess--though also old--haha!), simply because I found him rather annoying, rather than scary like his previous 'old' incarnation. Nonetheless, I did laugh when his insecurities showed, especially when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ he turned up shirtless, thinking Sophie would like him more if he styled himself like Tedros. That was hilarious.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />A character I would have liked to have learnt more about was the Good Brother. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ We never even learnt his name!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I was interested in his relationship with Rafal. Then again, I don't feel any worse for not knowing.<br /><br />Some people may find themselves a bit unsure of the messages the book puts across. Some might find the book too conservative, others too progressive. Throughout the book, I was constantly in debate with myself as to whether the messages of the story were positive or negative (from a liberal viewpoint)--certainly, most were positive, in my opinion, (and delightfully progressive at times too!) but I'm still mulling over Agatha's fate and whether I liked it or not. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ As much as I grew to like Tedros, I would have loved to have seen Agatha and Sophie BOTH being deans, together, at least for a little while--that would have been fab! Also, concerning Tedros and Agatha: WHAT IS THIS TALK OF BABIES LIKE THEY ARE ABSOLUTELY NECESSARY AT THIS POINT IN THEIR LIVES??? (I found that a bit weird...) Then again, this IS a fairytale at the end of the day, and the book stresses the importance of making sure you don't rush into a serious relationship, highlighting Tedros' parents as an example, which was definitely a good message.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Whatever the case, I like a book that makes me think, and this is certainly one of them. And it IS more progressive than not, especially for a kid's book, which is great to see. Good and evil, male and female, old and young--all these concepts are challenged in this seriously cool book.<br /><br />Sophie's ending was especially well done, and I really loved her relationship with Lady Lesso, who is now one my favourite characters. Sophie has always been a great character, so cruel yet so lovable at the same time. Even though on many an occasion I found myself screaming at her for acting idiotically, I understood why she behaved the way she did. Now I come to think of it, the ring, in a way, represented the vicious cycle she was caught in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ concerning her mother; by destroying the ring, she destroyed the cycle, and was able to find the happy ending her mother never found because she, unlike Vanessa, finally understood what true love was--and more importantly what it wasn't.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This was a nice touch, and I reckon Sophie will inspire kids who feel like they are trapped in a way of life from which they cannot escape to believe in themselves and break free.<br /><br />There is probably more I could say, but this is already fairly long and it's nearly 1am. In conclusion, I gave this book five-stars because any kid's book that can keep a nineteen-year-old student gripped to the point they only force themselves to put it down when they realise it's four in the morning--picking it up again as soon as they wake up, of course--is a winner.<br /><br />OH!<br /><br />And one last thing.<br />The last line is beyond fabulous. It captures the character of who says it so well--and it also captures the ultimate message of the story: Be yourself, love yourself, have faith in yourself. Maybe the end of your tale doesn't involve running off into the sunset with a prince, but that doesn't make it any less of a happily ever after.<br /><br />...THE END<br /><br /><b> 17/05/2016 EDIT </b><br />Changing this to four stars after much thought. Still love the twists, the humour etc but at the same time I feel the book could have been a wee bit shorter. Also, I do wish the possibility of an LGBT+ relationship had been explored further - it's so rare in middle grade. I'll end on a positive note though: the more I think about it, the gladder I am Sophie didn't end up with Hort, as much as I liked him as a character. A guy doesn't deserve a girl just because he is nice to her, and it seemed obvious to me Sophie didn't like him as much as he liked her. Soman Chainani handled that very well, I think :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1349215162194291827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17905906738611163563">For some reason it took me a while to get invested in this story but once I hit page 250 or so it picked up. I also believe that these books are meant for marathon reading sessions and not a few pages here and there. If you spend an hour or so reading and get deeper into the story and pace the book reads better. <br/><br/>In terms of character arc and development I still love Agatha and even Tedros but Sophie's overall journey was just meh. I was pretty unimpressed with her "growth" and found the ending a</span>
  <span id="freeText17905906738611163563" style="display:none">For some reason it took me a while to get invested in this story but once I hit page 250 or so it picked up. I also believe that these books are meant for marathon reading sessions and not a few pages here and there. If you spend an hour or so reading and get deeper into the story and pace the book reads better. <br /><br />In terms of character arc and development I still love Agatha and even Tedros but Sophie's overall journey was just meh. I was pretty unimpressed with her "growth" and found the ending a bit unrealistic for her. That said, the ending was rather predictable and not even the twists in Saders fairy tale reveal seemed original. But overall I really enjoyed this book and thought it was a fitting end to the series though I hear there may be more. <br /><br />Long live Queen Sophie. :) </span>

<div id="review_822293882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/822293882" />
    <a title="Pinky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky"><img alt="Pinky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489855494p2/27523984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/822293882?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pinky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pinky" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky">Pinky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27523984-pinky?shelf=books-i-want-to-own">books-i-want-to-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer822293882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8036056727174860101"> I have been in a reading slump for two and a half weeks! That's crazy, I can't believe I haven't read in so long. Nowadays, I have so many things to catch up on but there is NO TIME! Before I get too into my ranting, I want to talk to you about something. It's something that I have been thinking about for awhile.<br/> <br/> There are so many books and movies that have Good vs Evil. And if you think about it, MOST people, not all, support Good. While others support Evil, but in the end, Good always wins. </span>
  <span id="freeText8036056727174860101" style="display:none"> I have been in a reading slump for two and a half weeks! That's crazy, I can't believe I haven't read in so long. Nowadays, I have so many things to catch up on but there is NO TIME! Before I get too into my ranting, I want to talk to you about something. It's something that I have been thinking about for awhile.<br> <br> There are so many books and movies that have Good vs Evil. And if you think about it, MOST people, not all, support Good. While others support Evil, but in the end, Good always wins. But, have you ever thought about a world without Good? A world full of Evil, murders and crimes? Scary right? If there is no Good to stop the terrible acts, are the Evil really Evil? If there was a planet that had all Evil people and there were no Good people, were they considered to be Evil? Or is it normal to be Evil in that planet.<br><br> I know what you must be thinking, over the past two and a half weeks, I went bonkers. And now I am back with a crazy brain thinking about weird scenarios and questions. I have always wondered what it would be like if there was no such thing as Good. If the world was Evil, what would happen? Wouldn't it be normal to be Evil in a world of Evil?<br><br> Anyway, I really want to talk about this in more depth, and I could go on all day, so I am going onto the review. :)<br><br> <i>
  <b>“Of all the tales in all the kingdoms in all the Woods, you had to walk into mine.”</b>
</i><br><br> The School for Good and Evil is a trilogy and this is the final installment to the series. Every year, two kids are chosen/kidnapped from Gavaldon to a place. This year, Sophie and Agatha are chosen and are led to a school which has two different parts, the School for Evil and the School for Good. Sophie, the blond pretty girl strongly feels that she will be put in the School for Good while Agatha, the girl who is ignored with short, black hair feels that she might be put into the School for Evil. But instead of these things happening, the two girls are put unexpectedly in different schools. Sophie is in the School for Evil and Agatha is in the School for Good. The two girls go on a wild adventure in order to find out who they really are.<br><br> <i>
  <b> “But sometimes to keep Evil from getting in, you have to let Good out.” </b>
</i><br><br> After reading this book, it answered most of my weird questions that I asked at the beginning of this review. It showed me how a world would be like if it were Evil. I loved seeing the different details that made a difference to the world. It was interesting to see the different fairy tale villains, I loved it so much. Reading this book was so much fun and I am so sad that the series is finished.<br><br> <i>
  <b>“Dear girl, it will be a very long road if you spend more time looking backwards than forward.” </b>
</i><br><br> Another part of this book was the confusion between Agatha and Sophie and which one of them was going to be left out. Which girl did Tedros want to be with? Who was going to be left out, the third wheel? And it was really painful to see both of these characters suffering because they felt so alone. I felt like I could relate to these characters in this situations because I always feel alone. Maybe not in the same way as them, but the feelings that they went through were things I went through or currently go through. I hate that feeling and I kept thinking about how these characters should just forget everything and move on.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413735148ra/11555498.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> I loved all of the characters except for Rafal, of course. Tedros is super nice, although him and Agatha argue a lot. Agatha is a character that I most relate to and I understood her feelings of confusion for her future. Although Sophie was a bit annoying, I still loved her. Hort was hilarious and I couldn't stop laughing at him. I don't know why but Merlin reminds me of Dumbledore. There are just so many characters, it is hard to name all of them. But Rafal was so annoying and I just wanted to finish him off right away. He's so old, like he's older than my grandparents and yet he is flirting with teenagers. UGH!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450553025ra/17442242.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <i>
  <b>“This was about two sides warring for love."</b>
</i><br><br> Although the ending was sad, I loved it because everything ended perfectly. All of the conflicts were solved and we got to see a bit of everything. I wished I could read more, because there could have been a little bit more with Tedro, Agatha and Sophie and how they are in present day. But I loved the ending and it was such a solid conclusion. Soman Chainani did an awesome job on finishing this trilogy and I am so happy to have come across it.<br><br> <i>
  <b>“To find a happy ending with someone else, first you have to find it alone.”</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8036056727174860101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11664649366552802807"><br/>This would have gotten a higher rating if it hadn't been so bloody long. And angsty! -_-<br/>Full review to come.<br/><br/><a href='http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a> <br/><br/> Let me tell you that this book starts in an amazing way: Have you ever wondered what happens after a supposedly "happy ever after"?<br/>Well look no further, this story's beginning definitely focus on that part of Agatha and Tedros story.<br/>Is it all flowers and fluffy kittens?<br/>Well... no.<br/>After all Agatha does live in a cemetery and her cat <s>that bald and wrinkly thing</s> has very specific tastes</span>
  <span id="freeText11664649366552802807" style="display:none"><br>This would have gotten a higher rating if it hadn't been so bloody long. And angsty! -_-<br>Full review to come.<br><br><a href="http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415553706i/11810191.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br> Let me tell you that this book starts in an amazing way: Have you ever wondered what happens after a supposedly "happy ever after"?<br>Well look no further, this story's beginning definitely focus on that part of Agatha and Tedros story.<br>Is it all flowers and fluffy kittens?<br>Well... no.<br>After all Agatha does live in a cemetery and her cat <s>that bald and wrinkly thing</s> has very specific tastes: He's not a fan of princesses and princes -_-<br><br>So once again the author <u>picks up in a bunch of stereotypes and gives them a swift kick in the head.</u><br>It's great! ;)<br><br>By now you're probably wondering if I found this part so great, why did I gave it only a three star rating...<br>Well,... <u>THE STORY IS BLOODY LONG!</u><br>And it gets being long, by constantly undermining all that is happening. It got frustrating. It got tiresome.<br>By the middle of the thing I was ranting with the book: there was a couple of dozens of pages... strike that, make that two/ three hundred pages that should have been cut!<br>Longer isn't better, when you start getting annoyed by the constant back and forward sentimental activity <s>messing with your feelings</s> that the author introduced here. There were times I felt I was reading a New Adult novel with a very twisted love triangle. Argh.<br><br>The introduction of the "old" fairy tale characters was a good point: the interaction between our new heroes and the others provided some comic realief... exception made to the moments that were heartbreaking.<br><br>I liked that once again the author made sure to spread a lot of positive messages throughout the whole story:<br>_ No to body shaming.<br>_Yes to friendship.<br><br>The biggest problem for me and the reason why this gets only a three star, is that despite all the positive messages that this has, I cannot help ignore, that the main subject of the book, the relationship between Agatha, Sophie and Tedros ended up being a big mess. Especially when it comes to Sophie's part. After all that she had been through, I was expecting more from her: More growth, less idiocy.<br>What she does to her "friends" is not something a friend would do. And if that could be explained by where she ends up by the end of the story, I was never fully convinced of what ends up happening.<br><br>As for other positives, there was this twist, that I never saw coming, and that I loved.<br>Really well done, that.<br><br>Author's Official Site</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18309551327387351786"><b> Re-read(9-12-20) </b><br/><br/><br/>This book was good. It really tied everything together so nicely and gave a very satisfying ending. My problems with this book were mostly that so much was happening that is could have been spread out into two books and given us more fleshed out scenes and details. The pacing was also kinda wonky, with some parts feeling repetitive and slow, and other parts passin</span>
  <span id="freeText18309551327387351786" style="display:none"><b> Re-read(9-12-20) </b><br /><br /><br />This book was good. It really tied everything together so nicely and gave a very satisfying ending. My problems with this book were mostly that so much was happening that is could have been spread out into two books and given us more fleshed out scenes and details. And if not, shortening the book would have been acceptable, because this book book felt too long. A litteral brick. The pacing was also kinda wonky, with some parts feeling repetitive and slow, and other parts passing by too quickly when I wanted more. Overall I honestly would have been happy if this book was the finale of the series, but I am excited to re-read the Camelot years and I hope they exceed my expectations or at the very least meets my already existing expectations from my first read.<br /><br /><b> Also, I don't know how many times I have to say this but I need more Hester, Anadil, and Dot! </b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1948406731" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1948406731" />
    <a title="Sara Saif" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33555642-sara-saif"><img alt="Sara Saif" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567114974p2/33555642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1948406731?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Saif" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Saif" href="/user/show/33555642-sara-saif">Sara Saif</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=seriously-so-good-i-can-t-even">seriously-so-good-i-can-t-even</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1948406731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2710450930031098242"><p>That was a little above 3.5 stars which I’ll graciously round up to 4 because I’m a good person and also because the book was extremely easy to read, the silliness and hilarity helping despite being comparatively less amusing.</p><br/>I won’t be using phrases like “fitting finale” or “spectacular conclusion” to describe this last book in the trilogy owing to the fact that it was not. It wasn’t bad by any means. Fitting, perhaps, but certainly not spectacular and herein lies my disappointment. It was just</span>
  <span id="freeText2710450930031098242" style="display:none"><p>That was a little above 3.5 stars which I’ll graciously round up to 4 because I’m a good person and also because the book was extremely easy to read, the silliness and hilarity helping despite being comparatively less amusing.</p><br>I won’t be using phrases like “fitting finale” or “spectacular conclusion” to describe this last book in the trilogy owing to the fact that it was not. It wasn’t bad by any means. Fitting, perhaps, but certainly not spectacular and herein lies my disappointment. It was just plain <i>odd</i>.<br><p>A major thing that contributed to me being significantly less satisfied, charmed and more ‘meh’-ed was the back and forth in this series, particularly in the last one. There was just SO much repetition when it came to the question of characters’ personalities and their allegiances. The first one and maybe even the second one gave more than enough ground to cover that but to my EXTREME annoyance, it continued throughout this one too.</p><br>All it did, to me at least, was to make the protagonists, especially Sophie, murkier and more confusing than they were before. I couldn’t quite grasp what her actual deal was, though not for lack of trying. One second she’s Good, next she’s Evil, one second she’s complex and conflicted with a lot of grey areas, the next she’s just simply awful. I said it before and I’ll say it again, MAKE UP YOUR DAMN MIND. If it isn’t about who we are but what we do then why did Sophie despite trying her level best to be Good, kept doing bad things because she was Evil from the inside. Dude, that is the EXACT opposite of your actions making the difference, it’s who you are from the inside DICTATING your actions.<br><p>SO. MUCH. BACK. AND. FORTH:</p><br>Agatha and Tedros. Tedros and Sophie. Sophie and Agatha. Agatha and Tedros. Tedros and Sophie. Sophie and Agatha. My brain, my brain, MY TINY BRAIN. Ugh. It hurts. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490544896ra/22322648.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p>The book was darker than the previous ones but even though it tried to be more mature (through teenage angst, no less), the juvenile ‘air’ still lingered. All three of our heroes are 16 now but try as I might, I could not take them seriously. The irony here is amazing. I read <i>the School for Good and Evil</i> thinking that they were sixteen when in fact they were thirteen or fourteen. Here, they were <i>actually</i> sixteen but I kept seeing them as thirteen or fourteen.</p><br>The most mysterious and intriguing thing was Sophie and Agatha’s parents’ past and that kept me excited to know more. That and why the school master was interested in Gavaldon. These revelations made sense but I wasn’t completely blown away, ya know?<br><p>I also noticed two things that kept happening throughout the book:<br>a)	Tedros and other guys are mostly shirtless in every scene.<br>b)	Tedros and some other people (Agatha and Sophie) sweat up a storm like they have faulty skin that leaks too much.<br>But mainly, Tedros did both of these things and he did them again and again and again. Oh, look at Tedros and his perfectly ripped, tan stomach. Oh look, Tedros is sweating, his rumpled shirt is <i>drenched</i> in sweat, showing off that smooth, jacked up body… I have a question: WHY?</p><br>Hester and Anadil came a long way, from being despicable villains to adorable witches. Hort and Dot went through some staggering transformations during the three books but both remained the loveable fools we knew them to be. Which is why I was beyond dismayed by how Hort was treated overall. He may have acted like a sycophant before (and with good reason) but he more than proved himself here and still that wasn’t enough. Poor baby.<br><p>These books try to add to the concept of happily ever after and transform it to include more than just a girl meeting a boy. It’s a nice message, that girls don’t <i>always</i> or <i>necessarily</i> need boys to be happy. They can manage that well enough on their own if they want to. And that realizing your worth and being true to who you are is more important. But… it gets lost in the befuddlement of it all!</p><br>Here’s Agatha and Sophie’s entire journey as I saw it:<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<p><u>BOOK ONE:</u></p>
<br>Sophie: <i>I want to go to the School for Good and I want a prince.</i><br>Agatha: <i>I want Sophie, the rest of the world can go to blazes.</i><br>Tedros: <i>DAYUM, that Sophie chick is so fine. And who is that ugly crow?</i><br>Sophie: <i>I’m turning Evil! But, but I want to be Good! And where is that prince I asked for?</i><br>Agatha: <i>Everything sucks and I want Sophie.</i><br>Tedros: <i>Agatha. No, I mean Sophie. Obviously.</i><br>Sophie: <i>DEFINITELY EVIL. HATE AGATHA. WANT PRINCE. DIE, DIE, DIE.</i><br>Agatha: <i>Sophie just went batshit crazy. Can I have the prince now?</i><br>Tedros: <i>Sophie just went batshit crazy. Can I have the ugly crow, uh, I mean, Agatha now?</i><br>Sophie: <i>I want to be Good. I do not want a prince. AGATHA!</i><br>Agatha: <i>I hear you, Sophie, my best friend, my love. Let us leave this wretched place and find happily ever after specifically with each other! Oh, means I have to ditch Tedros. Huh.</i><br>Tedros: …<br>Agatha: <i>Oh well. See ya wouldn’t wanna be ya.</i><br>Sophie: <i>I AM GOOD AGAIN.</i><br>Tedros: <i>Wut.</i><br><p><u>BOOK TWO:</u></p>
<br>Sophie: <i>Every thing’s perfect. I have Agatha. Agatha has me. This is our Ever after.</i><br>Agatha: <i>Every thing’s perfect. I have Sophie. Sophie has me. This is our Ever after.</i><br>Tedros: <i>Dat bitch, Agatha. KISS her.</i><br>Sophie: <i>La-di-da.</i><br>Agatha: <i>Every thing’s not perfect. I don’t want Sophie. THIS is our Ever After. Yikes.</i><br>Tedros: <i>Dat bitch, Sophie. KILL her.</i><br>Sophie: <i>AGATHA YOU LYING WENCH. MUST KEEP HER AWAY FROM HER PRINCE.</i><br>Agatha: <i>Okay, I admit it, I want the pretentious sweat bag.</i><br>*An eavesdropping, a misunderstanding and a betrayal later.*<br>Tedros: <i>Those bitches. KILL THEM BOTH.</i><br>Sophie and Agatha: <i>FOR THE LAST TIME, THIS IS OUR HAPPILY EVER AFTER, DAMMIT.</i><br>Agatha and Tedros: <i>Nope.</i><br>Sophie: <i>DAYUM, that Tedros dude is so fine.</i><br>Agatha: <i>SOPHIE, YOU LYING WENCH.</i><br>Tedros and Agatha: <i>*smooch smooch*</i><br>Sophie: <i>Oh look, I’m Evil again.</i><br>(Me: Jeez, Sophie, make up your mind.)<br>Agatha: <i>SOPHIE, NO!</i><br>Tedros: <i>Jeez, Agatha, make up your mind.</i><br><p><u>BOOK THREE:</u></p>
<br>Agatha and Tedros: <i>Miss Sophie. Want Sophie.</i><br>Sophie: <i>I definitely want to be Good. I miss my besties. That school master is hawt.</i><br>School Master: <i>You’re Evil, honey. Accept it and save everyone the pain of figuring you out.</i><br>Sophie: <i>Mmmkay.</i><br>Agatha and Tedros: <i>Sophie is a Good person inside. We must get her back!</i><br>Sophie: <i>WTF are you two even doing here? Never mind, just listen. My heart beats for you, Tedros! Screw this newborn school master. I want to be your princess! Because you are my true love.</i><br>Agatha: <i>Oh, shit.</i><br>Tedros: <i>I will give you a chance, Sophie! (whispers: *I’m kidding, Agatha*) You are Good. Isn’t she totally Good, Agatha?</i><br>Agatha: …<br>Sophie: <i>YAY. I’m Good again!</i><br>(* a breakup, several seduction attempts and a couple of epiphanies later*)<br>Tedros: <i>Lol, Sophie, GET A LIFE.</i><br>Sophie: <i>*ovaries, stomach, chest, heart and eyes hardening* AYE.EM.EVILLLLLLLLLLLL. (For Good this time srsly promise) MUAHAHAHAHA.</i><br>Agatha: <i>SOPHIE, NO.</i><br>School Master: <i>Told ya so.</i><br>Sophie: <i>Yes, yes you did. I get it now. YOU are my true love. Not Agatha not Tedros. YOU!</i><br>Agatha: <i>Sophie, don’t be Evil. Our whole world depends on it.</i><br>Tedros: <i>Our whole world is SO screwed.</i><br>Sophie and Agatha: <i>*last minute emotional dialogue*</i><br>Sophie: <i>Here, the world is saved. Wait. Does that mean I’m Go-</i><br>Everyone: SHUT THE FUCK UP, SOPHIE.<br>Agatha: <i>You are meant to be with me, Sophie. We’re sisters!</i><br>Sophie: <i>But we kissed and thought our ever after was with each other!</i><br>Tedros: <i>YIKES.</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><p>So there you go. I hope that clears up why I was so frustrated the entire time.</p><br>Sophie and Agatha’s “relationship” throughout the book had me like:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490544896ra/22322647.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And Sophie being Good or Evil:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490544896ra/22322649.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p>Sophie and Agatha’s track is a fine example of writers not planning the end game and making it up as they go. I was way past the point of caring about them being together and that too a long time ago (because I shipped Tedros and Agatha) but I didn’t expect to be given something that would completely trump whatever came before it. Like, are we seriously expected to believe that?</p><br>Also, let me take a paragraph to express how utterly PISSED I was that Tedros and Sophie had started considering each other best friends? ARE. YOU. NUTS? They spent legit 3 days and 3 nights together half of which were spent as enemies. The other half consisted of trying to stay alive and like, 15 minutes sitting on a balcony together and saying deep things. 15 minutes. <b>15 MINUTES.</b> And might I add, the second Tedros found out that Finn was actually Sophie, he immediately FLIPPED OUT and rejected her. <b>BEST FRIENDS, MY FOOT.</b><br><p>Oh, sweet Catharsis. I feel so much better now. <br>I’ll say it again if anyone’s having trouble deciding whether this is a positive or a negative review: It’s a bit of both. The rating stars and review BOTH reflect how I feel, not just the stars. I enjoyed reading <i>the Last Ever After</i> but I had my problems with it and what better way to share those problems than write them up as long and vehemently as possible in your review? My review, my fingers, my rules.</p></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1105215547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1105215547" />
    <a title="Shadowdenizen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19784576-shadowdenizen"><img alt="Shadowdenizen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441031497p2/19784576.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1105215547?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shadowdenizen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shadowdenizen" href="/user/show/19784576-shadowdenizen">Shadowdenizen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19784576-shadowdenizen?shelf=fairy-tales-mythology">fairy-tales-mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1105215547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6482737989582092552">I'm not sure where to begin with this review...<br/><br/>As a whole, I'd give this series 4-stars, with some deep reservations. (I think this was a series with a high-profile premise, that you don't see too often in the genre, and that's what's carried me through the series, despite the almost rushed feel of the actual books.)<br/><br/>Soman Chanani succeeds wildly on several fronts:<br/>-Both Sophie and Agatha (our heroines) are well-drawn characters that you can immediately empathize with, and understand why they're f</span>
  <span id="freeText6482737989582092552" style="display:none">I'm not sure where to begin with this review...<br /><br />As a whole, I'd give this series 4-stars, with some deep reservations. (I think this was a series with a high-profile premise, that you don't see too often in the genre, and that's what's carried me through the series, despite the almost rushed feel of the actual books.)<br /><br />Soman Chanani succeeds wildly on several fronts:<br />-Both Sophie and Agatha (our heroines) are well-drawn characters that you can immediately empathize with, and understand why they're friends, which is crucial to the success of the series as a whole.<br />-The premise is intrguing, about 2 girls trying to find their place in the world and with each other, while still trying to find love and live within the "Fairy-Tale World" they become embroiled in. (A large part of the series revolves around pushing [or breaking] the boundaries of fairy-tale tropes.)<br />- Inclusiveness; this book feels very inclusive of all POV's regarding sexuality (while not a "Sexual/Adult" book [it's more about the IDEAL of "Love" in all it's forms], there are defintely undercurrents that were explored in this book, as in all the best fairy tales. (Look at the tale of Red Riding Hood if you doubt.)<br />-The Ending: Though it took a long time to get there, I thought the ending was perfect, and a much needed change from fairty-tale tropes. [At the risk of dating myself, it reminded me of the Kelly Taylor's "I choose myself" speech from the original Beverly Hills 90210.] And the final line? The perfect underscore for the series.<br /><br />The author also fails wildly on several fronts:<br />- Rushed and disjointed set-pieces. The comparison I liken this to is Harry Potter; via the slow-build-up we get to learn about Hogwarts as Harry does, and meet people as he does. The first few books serve as a great introduction to the series, and set-ups up what's to come. With this trilogy, despite the strong opening chapters in the first book, you are thrown right into the action, and it feels like giant pieces are "missing" to get to the next important set-pience of the story. (In particular, lessons and learning are almost incidental; Sophie and Agatha go from "School Newbies" to "Spell-Throwing witches" almost immediately, to the point where even the Teachers can't effectively challenge them.)<br />-Less delineated secondary characters. WHille there is a core cast of supporting/tertiary characters that recur througout the series, none of them are defined particualrly well, except by their relation to our heroines. (Though they did at least attempt to give Hort a convinving story-arc.) The Teachers are perhaps the most mis-used of this group, as they are almost completely interchangable, uninteresting, and ultimately irrelevant. [AS shown in Book 2, when ALL THE MALE TEACHERS are able to be put into an induced sleep-state for MOST OF THE BOOK!]<br />-POV: The narrative switch between Agatha and Sophie (when they're not together) happens at random intervals, and, while it's not hard to follow, it does serve to be a little jarring. I [personally] would have preferred an "Alternating Chapter" method to truly show the differences between the two charcters and schools.<br /><br />All said, though I enjoyed this trilogy more in theory than in actual execution, I would nonetheless recommend this to fans of fantasy &amp; fairy-tales, as well as those who like their fantasy fiction a bit on the subversive side. (Relations and friendships between same-sex characters in fantasy are not often dealt with in such a straightforward manner, and it was quite a refreshing change.)<br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6482737989582092552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer422847520047133150">Ohhh so many things I want to say about this book, but I can't even find the right words to it!<br/>What a big mess! Sorry but, all the three books has the same end: no matter what, Sophie is evil and never will get what she wants. <br/>Which I think is really bad because, as Sophie try so hard to be good, which makes her be even more evil, it's like seeing evil winning, in the end!<br/>So, what good message does this book brings?! None!<br/>It's full of violence and no true love at all! A son killing his own mothe</span>
  <span id="freeText422847520047133150" style="display:none">Ohhh so many things I want to say about this book, but I can't even find the right words to it!<br />What a big mess! Sorry but, all the three books has the same end: no matter what, Sophie is evil and never will get what she wants. <br />Which I think is really bad because, as Sophie try so hard to be good, which makes her be even more evil, it's like seeing evil winning, in the end!<br />So, what good message does this book brings?! None!<br />It's full of violence and no true love at all! A son killing his own mother (Alric and Lady Lesso), a father trying to kill her own daughter (Stephan and Agatha)... how "nice", huh? But it's ok, since we have the excuse that are the Good and Evil sides, here! <br />I just read this book, because of curiosity to know how would end it. And I was hoping that, atleast, it was going to have a true happy ending but, like I said, everything just repeated as happened in the previews books.<br />The writer reaaally didn't make it works! C'mon! The two girls, best friends, had their kiss in the end of the first book and now, to worse, they are sisters?!<br />I love retellings, but the writer ruined with everything, here! Cinderella wanting just their stepsisters' love.. ok, I can accept that, but being killed by axe by his stepmother... WOW! That's really too much! <br />Which also reminds me how this book is a "good" reading to children! <br />Honestly... what a hideous book!</span>

<div id="review_1146854179" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1146854179" />
    <a title="Annabelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27883570-annabelle"><img alt="Annabelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456180742p2/27883570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1146854179?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annabelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annabelle" href="/user/show/27883570-annabelle">Annabelle</a>
      </span>

<div id="review_1762152861" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1762152861" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38672507-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474291977p2/38672507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1762152861?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/38672507-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1762152861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14988313945468936774">I have one question that I think completely summarises my thoughts:<br/><b>WHY THE FUCK IS THIS THING 650 PAGES LONG?!</b><br/><br/>Seriously. I could end my review there and I think it would be adequate. But I'm not going to do that because I actually have a lot to say about this book. My list of complaints is quite lengthy so prepare yourselves. <br/><br/>BUT FIRST, some background information. I think the first book in this series was excellent! Its commentary on Good vs Evil, destiny, friendship and happy endings was top n</span>
  <span id="freeText14988313945468936774" style="display:none">I have one question that I think completely summarises my thoughts:<br /><b>WHY THE FUCK IS THIS THING 650 PAGES LONG?!</b><br /><br />Seriously. I could end my review there and I think it would be adequate. But I'm not going to do that because I actually have a lot to say about this book. My list of complaints is quite lengthy so prepare yourselves. <br /><br />BUT FIRST, some background information. I think the first book in this series was excellent! Its commentary on Good vs Evil, destiny, friendship and happy endings was top notch and would make a great animated movie. The second book was much less good; it was Boys vs Girls and instead of making interesting observations about gender roles it was just super stereotyped and stupid so I didn't enjoy it all that much. I went into the third book not expecting anything great and I was still, somehow, let down by it. <b>So let's get this review going!!</b><br /><br /><b>Problem number ONE is the characters!</b> We have three main characters in this book and I only like one of them, Agatha. <b>Agatha is balanced, kind, passionate and caring</b> but also struggles in realistic ways (as any protagonist should). Tedros is honestly ridiculous for most of the story. I'll admit that by the end of the book he had somewhat redeemed himself but for the majority he was a spoiled child with a temper. He was <b>rude</b> to the girl he loved and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[never spoke with her about the fact that her mother died, even going so far as to make a joke about how ugly she had been (what a dreamboat!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. He was also quite sexist a lot of the time and just not an attractive character in general.<br /><br />Then there is Sophie. <b>Where do I even START with Sophie</b>! This book would have been 300 pages shorter if Sophie wasn't such a self-absorbed and impulsive character. And yes, I am well aware that she is meant to be Evil. But <b>her characterisation was incredibly inconsistent</b> and the change in her personality between scenes was often a little crazy. The thing is I really wanted to like Sophie; I really wanted to root for the character who is struggling to find and love herself but she just hopped between a few different personalities for what felt like the convenience of the plot. <b>Things are slowing down?</b> <i>Sophie is good again!</i> <b>Nothing for the characters to talk about?</b> <i>Well, better make Sophie Evil again!</i> And on and on and on like that... It was just infuriating. <br /><br />Much like Sophie's character development, <b>the plot also went in CIRCLES!</b> For a 650 page book there wasn't a whole lot that happened. A whole bunch of new characters were introduced, both sides train for the upcoming war, the three main characters struggle with their identities aaannnddd <i>that's about it</i>. There's bits and pieces of fighting but a lot of the story is based around whether Sophie is Good or Evil and which side she is going to take in the war. It was interesting at first but <b>there is only so much repetition I can handle</b>. Especially when the outcome of the story is so <b>predictable</b>... I mean, it's a middle-grade story so <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[of COURSE Sophie is going to end up being Good and Good will win over Evil. DUH <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />So yeah. I could keep complaining about this. I don't think the writing was great. The side characters weren't all that well-developed and the magic system was as vague as ever. There were also some side characters who seemed WAY more powerful than anyone else. <b>Some POSITIVES to end the review though:</b><br />- This final book does manage to have a darker tone and I really admire the author for doing that! There were some moments that completely took me by surprise.<br />- I think Agatha is an excellent character and she is what kept me reading! She is really well-developed and so lovable.<br />- The concept and creativity of this series! I may not have loved this book but there are a lot of cool bits and pieces in there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14988313945468936774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7978766627769343610"><a href='http://www.inkvotary.com/2017/07/the-last-ever-after-by-soman-chainani.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Inkvotary</a><br/>Finished. FINALLY! Way too long, way too detailed and way too much of everything. Tedros is a weak coward with no courage at all. Good looking but full of fear and ... I have no words. Right now I doubt that I will read the fourth book. Not after the torture this one was. How can a series, that startet so great and with a firework of fun, irony and great scenes become such a disaster? No recommendation from my side. Sorry, Mr. Chainani.</span>
  <span id="freeText7978766627769343610" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.inkvotary.com/2017/07/the-last-ever-after-by-soman-chainani.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Inkvotary</a><br />Finished. <div id="review_934029109" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/934029109" />
    <a title="Carina Olsen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5457171-carina-olsen"><img alt="Carina Olsen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566083624p2/5457171.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/934029109?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carina Olsen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carina Olsen" href="/user/show/5457171-carina-olsen">Carina Olsen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5457171-carina-olsen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer934029109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5956658300588872281">Reading this book for the fourth time and I'm still as heartbroken as the first time I read it. Ha. This third book is still my favorite of them all. It hurts in all the right places. Although I'm not sure my heart can take more. It's also the book with all the best endings. For so many of them. It is a book filled with hope for the future.<br/><br/>At the same time as they watch their world almost be destroyed for good. There is so much going on this book. All of it exciting and interesting to read about</span>
  <span id="freeText5956658300588872281" style="display:none">Reading this book for the fourth time and I'm still as heartbroken as the first time I read it. Ha. This third book is still my favorite of them all. It hurts in all the right places. Although I'm not sure my heart can take more. It's also the book with all the best endings. For so many of them. It is a book filled with hope for the future.<br /><br />At the same time as they watch their world almost be destroyed for good. There is so much going on this book. All of it exciting and interesting to read about. Agatha is still the most precious of them all, always. And Sophie is still fully complicated. I hated her the most in this one. Yet I still love her too, at times. Mostly.<br /><br />The writing is still perfect, of course. Though I'm still confused about how time is working in these books, ha. It has not passed as much time as they are all claiming. Yet I don't mind this much at all. Too busy focusing on the amazing story. I shall not share too much about this precious book this time. Just sharing a little about how much I love it. It is the book that brings me the most pain. But it is also the book that makes me the most happy. All the Agatha and Tedros scenes are so good. First so painful and hurtful. Then so hopeful, precious, lovely and romantic. Their romance is the best thing. And the friendship between Agatha and Sophie is so good too. Though I may have wanted Sophie dead for most of the book. Oops. But even so. I loved her as well.<br /><br />This book is about the war between the old villains and everyone else. It is about Agatha learning to love herself like she should. About her learning to set herself first at times, although she pretty much never do this. Agatha is the most good person in all of these books. And I loved her so very much because of this. She deserves all the love and all the happy endings possible. And I still want Tedros to give her the world. So fingers crossed for that in the next books, haha. I just. Agatha is the very best and I love her so much.<br /><br />Then there was Sophie. Having chosen the young evil school master as her love. This does not go well. And Sophie changes so much. She gets so evil at times. It's heartbreaking to read about. As all she really wants is to be loved. Not to end up alone. But she chooses all the wrong ways to get her happy ending. She hurts many people. Agatha most of all. I will probably never forgive Sophie for trying to take Tedros away from Agatha. And not even feeling a little bit sorry about it. Hmph. Yeah, I am a little angry with her.<br /><br />But gosh, how good this book is. We see more of the famous fairy tales. Meet some of the older heroes from those tales and their villains too. This book is so dark at times. I loved it so. It focuses on them all trying to save the fairy tale world from ending. Well, the good people trying to save it anyway. So many secrets are revealed. I loved the story about Sophie's mother. Heartbreaking but good. I loved learning everything in this book. So much is revealed. All of it awesome. How I love all of the side characters too.<br /><br />I could probably talk about this book forever and ever. But not sharing much more about it. I just love it so very much. I love the relationships between them all. I so love the amazing friendships. I love the schools and the teachers. They are all awesome. Most of all I love reading about Agatha. Sigh. Though I feel like maybe the death of her mother should have been bigger, aka more grief. Still. It was still written so well. And I just love this world to death. I cannot wait to read even more about it. So excited for the next books.<br /><br />The Last Ever After is still the most perfect book to me. Completely heartbreaking and evil. Fully hopeful and good. This book has it all. It still hurts my heart the most to read through the beginning. Agatha is in so much pain. It is the worst. But still the best too. Sigh. I simply love Agatha too much, haha. I cannot stand seeing her in pain. Hmph. But yes. This book still means everything to me. It is still my favorite of them all. Though I haven't read book five and six yet, so it might change. But I doubt it. This is perfection.<br /><br />There is so much I love about these books. The gorgeous covers. I mean, come on. They are stunning. I love the illustrations in the beginning of each chapter. So precious. I love this fairy tale world. Adore these amazing characters and how different they are. I love that this is a story about good and evil. And how it's possible to be both at times. I'm so glad I found these books. So glad I'm reading them again now. I know that I will still read them again and again. If you still haven't started, you are missing out on the best story.<br /><br /><i>And because Sophie knew that deep, deep down, in the pit of her soul, Agatha was Good. And when put to the test, Agatha would sacrifice everything to stay true to that Good. Even if it meant surrendering her battle to win the war. Even if it meant giving up her prince. Even if it meant her prince giving up her.</i><br /><br />---<br /><br />I first read this book from August 9th to August 10th 2015. See my first review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://carinabooks.blogspot.no/2015/08/review-last-ever-after-by-soman-chainani.html">http://carinabooks.blogspot.no/2015/0...</a><br /><br />I read this book for the second time from July 27th to July 30th 2016. See my book recommendation post here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://carinabooks.blogspot.no/2016/07/book-recommendation-last-ever-after-by.html">http://carinabooks.blogspot.no/2016/0...</a><br /><br />I read this book for the third time from October 3rd to 5th 2017. See my new review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://carinabooks.blogspot.no/2017/10/review-last-ever-after-by-soman-chainani.html">http://carinabooks.blogspot.no/2017/1...</a><br /><br />I read this book for the fourth time from July 12th to 16th 2020. See my new review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://carinabooks.blogspot.com/2020/07/review-last-ever-after-by-soman-chainani.html">https://carinabooks.blogspot.com/2020...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5956658300588872281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1824657972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1824657972" />
    <a title="Angela Auten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54842999-angela-auten"><img alt="Angela Auten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484022621p2/54842999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1824657972?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela Auten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela Auten" href="/user/show/54842999-angela-auten">Angela Auten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/26050812-the-last-ever-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54842999-angela-auten?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54842999-angela-auten?shelf=paperback-books">paperback-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54842999-angela-auten?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54842999-angela-auten?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54842999-angela-auten?shelf=want-to-re-read">want-to-re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1824657972&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1824657972" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4956630349637032604">The Last Ever After Review<br/> <br/>Book Rating: 5 stars out 5. <br/><br/>Storyline: 5 stars out of 5. The last book in the School for Good and Evil trilogy. (I know there is a fourth one coming out! That starts a new chapter in the series! I'm excited for it!) It was a long journey. Sophie decided to be with the young school Master. Agatha and Tedros were in Gavaldon. The village tried to kill them. They went through Sophie's mother's grave to get back to the woods. They were met by Red Riding Hoods wolf and Jack</span>
  <span id="freeText4956630349637032604" style="display:none">The Last Ever After Review<br /> <br />Book Rating: 5 stars out 5. <br /><br />Storyline: 5 stars out of 5. The last book in the School for Good and Evil trilogy. (I know there is a fourth one coming out! That starts a new chapter in the series! I'm excited for it!) It was a long journey. Sophie decided to be with the young school Master. Agatha and Tedros were in Gavaldon. The village tried to kill them. They went through Sophie's mother's grave to get back to the woods. They were met by Red Riding Hoods wolf and Jack's giant. Princess Uma rescued them. She was bringing them to the league of good heroes. They met Cinderella, Peter Pan, Hansel and Gretel, etc. Agatha had to try to get Sophie to destroy the ring. That would kill the School Master. Sophie questions if she actually loves him. Tedros' name appears on her skin. Sophie runs away with Agatha and Tedros. She tries to convince Tedros to go out with her. He still loved Agatha. His mother, Guinevere, is also found as long as Lancelot. They shelter them from the School Master. Tedros asks Sophie why she wants to be with him. She doesn't tell him that she loves him. Tedros leaves her in the cave. She ends of going back to the school master. The league trains with the new heroes for the Good and Evil war. Sophie and Agatha find out through Professor Sader that they are sister's. That Vanessa was evil because she wished to be with Sophie's father when he was in love with Honora the whole time. Her mother gave birth to Sophie and Agatha. Agatha being the ugly one and Sophie being the beautiful one. Good and Evil go to war. Sophie decides to finally destroy the ring. The ending was interesting. There was a whole bunch of events. I loved this whole story. I can't wait to read the 4th one. I want it released right now! (It's released, but still haven't purchased it. I really should do that.) <br /><br />Characters: 5 stars out of 5. I loved Agatha the most out of this series. She was amazing. I loved her attitude. I'm glad that she got her prince in the end. She made so many sacrifices. She had more depth than Sophie. She was the good one. Always will be.<br /><br />Tedros was arrogant a lot, but he showed that he loved Agatha. He made some sacrifices as well. I didn't like him the first book. He got better in the last book. He was sweet at times. He was hard at times. <br /><br />Sophie...I wanted her to die. She was the worst character in this whole story. She should have been happy for her friend, but she wasn't. She was a brat that tried to steal her friends love. She thought she was amazing, but she was nothing. She was stupid. I really wished she died at the end. <br /><br />Favorite Quotes: “Dear girl, it will be a very long road if you spend more time looking backwards than forward.” <br /><br />“No one can hide from their fate without a price.”<br /><br />“To find a happy ending with someone else, first you have to find it alone.” <br /><br />Writing Style: 5 stars out of 5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4956630349637032604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
